[11] assistant
I reviewed `task_1_Task_list_pagination_fix_69f26715-2694-83eb-a4d0-d352889d75bb.messages`. Summary below. fileciteturn0file0 ## Critical assessment first The previous chat started as a narrow **task-list pagination and slow task selection bug**, but it grew into a broader Promptbranch architecture thread. The original issue was real: `pb task list` capped at 20 tasks, and `pb task use 4` was too slow because it still triggered expensive live enumeration/history paths. The later work shifted toward a safer local control-plane architecture: Promptbranch as its own MCP host/client, with read-only tools first, skills as workflow instructions, Ollama only as proposal/summarization, and write/process tools gated by policy. fileciteturn2file0 ## Original bugs ### Bug 1 — `pb task list` only showed 20 tasks The first report showed a project with more than 20 tasks, but `pb task list` returned exactly 20. Early diagnostics showed: ```text source_counts: snorlax = 20 dom = 10 history = 0 history_detail = 0 ``` The likely root causes investigated were bad pagination cursor handling, project-specific backend endpoint limitations, and fallback history scans that were slow but not productive. ### Bug 2 — `pb task use 4` was too slow `pb task use 4` selected the correct task but took minutes in the early versions because it still called the live task listing path and sometimes triggered slow history fallback. The eventual effective fix was **local per-project task-list caching**, so the common flow: ```bash pb task list pb task use 4 ``` could resolve from cache instead of calling the browser/service again. ## Release timeline ### v0.0.130 Started from `v0.0.129`. Added a project-specific conversation endpoint probe and changed `task use <index>` to prefer a lightweight indexed list. This was a reasonable first hypothesis, but live logs later showed the endpoint probe did not yet work correctly. ### v0.0.131 Fixed one endpoint-call mistake: the first request should not send `cursor=0`. Also changed default task listing to avoid global history probing unless explicitly requested through a deep-history mode. This reduced bad default behavior but did not fully solve either bug. ### v0.0.132 Added the per-project task-list cache in `.pb_profile`. This fixed the practical slow `pb task use 4` case after a prior `pb task list`. Bug 1 remained open because normal list output still capped at 20. ### v0.0.133 Adjusted `snorlax/sidebar` pagination to prefer the nested `conversations.cursor` instead of the root cursor. This was the right direction: the root cursor likely paginated projects/gizmos, while the nested cursor should paginate conversations inside the selected project. ### v0.0.134–v0.0.137 The chat temporarily shifted to source-add ergonomics and overwrite behavior: ```bash pbsa file.zip ``` became shorthand for: ```bash pbsa --file file.zip ``` Then default overwrite behavior was added for matching file sources: detect existing source, remove it, upload the replacement, and verify persistence. The major reliability lesson from this area was the **early refresh aborting save** failure: refreshing too soon after Save could race or abort the source upload/commit. The fix principle became: wait for dialog close, Sources idle state, Add button visibility, and a short dwell before persistence verification. fileciteturn1file5 ### v0.0.138–v0.0.141 The project moved into MCP scaffolding: ```bash pb agent inspect . --json pb agent doctor . --json pb agent plan "sync repo" --json pb mcp manifest --json pb mcp serve --path . pb mcp config --path . --json pb mcp host-smoke --path . --json ``` The design stayed intentionally read-only. Controlled/write tools could be listed only when explicitly requested, but execution remained blocked until policy gates and transactional verification existed. fileciteturn2file2 ### v0.0.146–v0.0.147 Ollama/tool-call work was added and then corrected. The key decision: **Ollama must not be trusted as the planner or executor**. It may propose one read-only tool call or summarize, but Promptbranch must classify the original request first and validate the model proposal before MCP execution. Invalid output fails closed. fileciteturn2file0 v0.0.147 fixed a parser bug where `--command` overwrote the root command field, and also fixed the integration-suite visibility rule so `project_endpoint` counted as indexed visibility. ### v0.0.148 This was the major local-agent milestone. Added: ```bash pb agent run "read VERSION and git status" --path . --json pb agent host-smoke --path . --json pb agent mcp-call filesystem.read '{"path":"VERSION"}' --path . --json pb skill list --json pb skill show repo-inspection --json pb skill validate .promptbranch/skills/repo-inspection --json pb agent run --skill repo-inspection "inspect repo" --path . --json ``` This aligned with the updated architecture: Promptbranch should become its own MCP host/client, with MCP providing deterministic local tools, skills guiding workflows, and Ollama remaining optional and untrusted. fileciteturn2file1 ### v0.0.149 Added the first controlled process tool: ```bash test.smoke ``` and wired: ```bash pb agent run "run smoke tests" --path . --json ``` to execute only a fixed bounded smoke command: ```bash promptbranch test smoke --json --only mcp_smoke --only mcp_host_smoke ``` The validation showed the intended safety boundary worked: `"run smoke tests"` was allowed as a controlled external process, while `"run pytest"` was rejected as uncontrolled. fileciteturn2file1 ## Current accepted baseline The current accepted baseline at the end of the previous chat is: ```text chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.149.zip ``` The next requested release is: ```text v0.0.150 ``` Scope already stated: ```text cleanup only: - rename controlled mode terminology from “writes” to “process” - fix timeout diagnostic reporting - keep source/artifact writes blocked ``` ## Architecture decisions carried forward Promptbranch should not try to become literal Claude Code. The chosen architecture is: ```text Promptbranch CLI / local host = control plane ChatGPT Project = workspace ChatGPT chat = task/session Project sources = repo snapshots/specs/logs MCP servers = deterministic local tools Ollama = optional proposal/summarization only Skills = validated workflow instructions ZIP artifacts = release outputs ``` The three state scopes are: ```text Workspace = current ChatGPT Project Task = current chat/conversation Artifact = current source bundle/release ZIP ``` State must not conflate these scopes. fileciteturn1file10 ## Main rules established Reads should be backend-first: ```text backend JSON / network payload → saved Promptbranch state → DOM fallback → OCR/image fallback only as last resort ``` Writes must be transactional: ```text trigger action → wait for settled/backend-confirmed state → re-read and verify persistence → update local state only after verification ``` Ollama must remain constrained: ```text deterministic planner chooses tools Ollama may propose/summarize only Promptbranch validates every proposal invalid/empty output fails closed no write/destructive execution from model proposals ``` Skills are not MCP servers. They are local, validated operating procedures that declare allowed tools and preconditions; they cannot bypass the policy gate. fileciteturn2file2 ## What is done ✅ `pb task use <index>` practical slowness was fixed through task-list cache. ✅ MCP read-only server and host-smoke paths exist. ✅ `pb agent run` exists for deterministic read-only local inspection. ✅ Local skill registry exists with `repo-inspection`. ✅ Ollama proposal flow exists but is gated. ✅ Controlled process execution exists for `test.smoke`. ✅ Arbitrary shell/process execution remains blocked. ✅ Source/artifact writes remain blocked from agent execution. ## What remains weak ⚠️ The original “more than 20 tasks” listing problem was improved diagnostically, but the uploaded chat does not prove a final robust >20 live enumeration fix. ⚠️ Naming is currently misleading: `read_only_plus_controlled_writes` should become `read_only_plus_controlled_process`. ⚠️ Timeout diagnostics are inconsistent: outer fields showed values like `65.0` and `8.0` while inner `test.smoke` used the correct `60.0`. ⚠️ Several releases used compile checks and direct assertions instead of full pytest because pytest hung in the container. ## Next step Create `chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.150.zip` from `chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.149.zip` only. Required changes: ```text 1. Rename controlled-write terminology to controlled-process terminology. 2. Fix timeout diagnostic reporting. 3. Keep source sync, artifact release, git writes, and project source mutation blocked. 4. Preserve all v0.0.149 behavior. 5. Package ZIP with repo contents at root level, no wrapper folder. ``` Verdict: ✅ Strengths — the workflow matured from a UI pagination bugfix into a safer backend-first, MCP-gated local control-plane design. ⚠️ Weaknesses — task-list pagination beyond 20 still needs live proof; some terminology and diagnostics are stale. 🔍 Unknowns — whether project task enumeration remains stable against ChatGPT backend/UI changes. 🧩 Next step — implement v0.0.150 cleanup from `v0.0.149`, with no new write capabilities.

[119] user
exec > >(tee -a "$LOG") 2>&1 can you make a bash script out of it so I can use it everywhere How do I stop this exec?

[120] assistant
What may fail first: `exec > >(tee -a "$LOG") 2>&1` changes stdout/stderr for the **current shell**. If you run it directly, every command keeps logging until you restore stdout/stderr or close that shell. ## Option 1 — safer universal wrapper script Create this file: ```bash mkdir -p ~/.local/bin nano ~/.local/bin/runlog ``` Paste: ```bash #!/usr/bin/env bash set -euo pipefail LOG_DIR="${LOG_DIR:-$PWD}" LOG_NAME="${LOG_NAME:-run_$(date +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S).log}" LOG_PATH="$LOG_DIR/$LOG_NAME" mkdir -p "$LOG_DIR" echo "Logging to: $LOG_PATH" if [ "$#" -eq 0 ]; then echo "No command supplied. Starting logged interactive shell." echo "Type 'exit' to stop logging." exec bash -i > >(tee -a "$LOG_PATH") 2>&1 else { echo "===== START $(date -Is) =====" echo "PWD: $PWD" echo "CMD: $*" echo "$@" status=$? echo echo "===== END $(date -Is), exit=$status =====" exit "$status" } > >(tee -a "$LOG_PATH") 2>&1 fi ``` Make it executable: ```bash chmod +x ~/.local/bin/runlog ``` Make sure `~/.local/bin` is on your PATH: ```bash echo 'export PATH="$HOME/.local/bin:$PATH"' >> ~/.bashrc source ~/.bashrc ``` Use it anywhere like this: ```bash runlog promptbranch agent host-smoke --path . --json ``` Or start a logged shell: ```bash runlog ``` Then run many commands. Stop logging by typing: ```bash exit ``` This is the safest pattern because the `exec` only affects the wrapper shell, not your original terminal session. ## Option 2 — start/stop logging in the current shell Add these functions to `~/.bashrc`: ```bash startlog() { local log_name="${1:-session_$(date +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S).log}" export LOG="$PWD/$log_name" exec 3>&1 exec 4>&2 exec > >(tee -a "$LOG") 2>&1 echo "Logging started: $LOG" echo "Run stoplog to restore normal stdout/stderr." } stoplog() { echo "Logging stopped: $LOG" exec 1>&3 exec 2>&4 exec 3>&- exec 4>&- unset LOG } ``` Reload: ```bash source ~/.bashrc ``` Use: ```bash startlog test_150_rerun.log # run commands stoplog ``` ## How to stop the original `exec` If you already ran: ```bash exec > >(tee -a "$LOG") 2>&1 ``` without saving file descriptors first, the practical stop options are: ```bash exit ``` or close that terminal tab/session. If you used the `startlog` function above, stop cleanly with: ```bash stoplog ``` Verdict: ✅ Best approach — use `runlog` as a wrapper; it is portable and does not poison your current shell. ⚠️ Weakness — `startlog`/`stoplog` only works if you start logging through the function. 🔍 Unknown — whether you use Bash or Zsh; the wrapper is Bash-compatible. 🧩 Next step — create `~/.local/bin/runlog` and use `runlog` before your Promptbranch test commands.

So v0.0.151 is intentionally narrow: **diagnostics and packaging hygiene only**, no new write/process capability. ## Changes made - Bumped version metadata to `v0.0.151`. - Fixed `mcp_host_smoke` so it no longer falls back to: ```text filesystem.read "." ``` - If `VERSION` or `README.md` is missing, host-smoke now returns: ```text status: read_target_missing ``` with repo path, candidate files, git-root diagnostic, and suggested path when available. - Added git-root-aware skill path resolution, so this works better from subdirectories: ```bash pb skill validate .promptbranch/skills/repo-inspection --path <subdir> --json ``` - Added packaging regression coverage for excluding: ```text .pytest_cache/ __pycache__/ *.pyc ``` - Removed pytest cache files from the generated release ZIP. ## Validation Passed: ```text 72 passed ``` for: ```bash pytest -q tests/test_promptbranch_mcp.py tests/test_promptbranch_artifacts.py tests/test_cli_parser.py ``` Also passed targeted version/container checks: ```text 3 passed ``` ZIP checks: ```text VERSION = v0.0.151 ZIP CRC/testzip = OK No .pytest_cache entries No __pycache__ entries No *.pyc entries No wrapper folder ``` Not claimed: a broader CLI/container test batch timed out, so I did not treat it as successful evidence. bash -lc cd /mnt/data/work_153 && python - <<'PY' from pathlib import Path p=Path('promptbranch_mcp.py') s=p.read_text() insert_after='''def _read_bounded_text(path: Path, *, max_bytes: int) -> dict[str, Any]:\n if not path.is_file():\n return {"ok": False, "error": "file_not_found", "path": str(path)}\n try:\n with path.open("rb") as handle:\n data = handle.read(max_bytes + 1)\n except OSError as exc:\n return {"ok": False, "error": str(exc), "path": str(path)}\n truncated = len(data) > max_bytes\n data = data[:max_bytes]\n try:\n text = data.decode("utf-8")\n encoding = "utf-8"\n except UnicodeDecodeError:\n text = data.decode("utf-8", errors="replace")\n encoding = "utf-8-replacement"\n return {\n "ok": True,\n "path": str(path),\n "encoding": encoding,\n "truncated": truncated,\n "bytes_returned": len(data),\n "text": text,\n }\n\n''' helper='''def _deterministic_log_summary(text: str, *, max_marker_lines: int = 12) -> dict[str, Any]:\n """Return a local read-only summary that does not depend on a model.\n\n This is deliberately heuristic. It gives the operator a useful result when\n Ollama is unavailable or slow, while preserving the safety rule that models\n cannot plan, execute, or mutate state.\n """\n\n lines = text.splitlines()\n lowered = text.lower()\n headings = [line.strip() for line in lines if line.strip().startswith("=====")][:20]\n marker_terms = (\n '"ok": false',\n '"status": "risk_rejected"',\n '"status": "path_outside_repo"',\n '"status": "summary_unavailable"',\n '"status": "error"',\n 'failed',\n 'failure',\n 'timed out',\n 'timeout',\n 'traceback',\n 'exception',\n 'error',\n )\n marker_lines: list[str] = []\n for line in lines:\n compact = line.strip()\n if not compact:\n continue\n lower = compact.lower()\n if any(term in lower for term in marker_terms):\n marker_lines.append(compact[:500])\n if len(marker_lines) >= max_marker_lines:\n break\n\n counts = {\n "ok_true": text.count('"ok": true'),\n "ok_false": text.count('"ok": false'),\n "verified": text.count('"status": "verified"'),\n "risk_rejected": text.count('"status": "risk_rejected"'),\n "path_outside_repo": text.count('"status": "path_outside_repo"'),\n "summary_unavailable": text.count('"status": "summary_unavailable"'),\n "timed_out": lowered.count("timed out") + lowered.count("timeout"),\n "traceback": lowered.count("traceback"),\n }\n hard_failure = bool(counts["traceback"] or counts["ok_false"] or counts["timed_out"] or "failed" in lowered or "exception" in lowered)\n if counts["risk_rejected"] and not counts["traceback"]:\n assessment = "contains expected policy rejections; inspect marker_lines for unexpected failures"\n elif hard_failure:\n assessment = "contains failure or timeout markers"\n else:\n assessment = "no obvious failure markers detected in bounded excerpt"\n\n return {\n "ok": True,\n "status": "generated",\n "method": "deterministic_heuristic_v1",\n "line_count": len(lines),\n "counts": counts,\n "headings": headings,\n "marker_lines": marker_lines,\n "assessment": assessment,\n }\n\n''' if helper in s: raise SystemExit('helper already present') s=s.replace(insert_after, insert_after+helper) # update function status and payload old=''' summary = _call_ollama_generate(\n prompt=prompt,\n model=model,\n host=ollama_host,\n timeout_seconds=ollama_timeout_seconds,\n num_predict=320,\n )\n return {\n "ok": True,\n "action": "agent_summarize_log",\n "status": "summarized" if summary.get("ok") else "summary_unavailable",\n "mode": "ollama_summary_read_only",\n "repo_path": str(root),\n "log_path": raw_path,\n "resolved_path": str(target),\n "read": {k: v for k, v in read_payload.items() if k != "text"},\n "ollama": {\n "used_for_planning": False,\n "used_for_summary": True,\n "model": model,\n "host": ollama_host,\n "summary": summary,\n "note": "Ollama summary failure is non-fatal; the log read metadata remains authoritative.",\n },\n "safety": {"repo_bound_read": True, "write_tools_blocked": True, "model_has_execution_authority": False},\n }\n''' new=''' deterministic_summary = _deterministic_log_summary(text[:max_bytes])\n summary = _call_ollama_generate(\n prompt=prompt,\n model=model,\n host=ollama_host,\n timeout_seconds=ollama_timeout_seconds,\n num_predict=320,\n )\n return {\n "ok": True,\n "action": "agent_summarize_log",\n "status": "summarized" if summary.get("ok") else "deterministic_summary",\n "mode": "ollama_summary_read_only",\n "repo_path": str(root),\n "log_path": raw_path,\n "resolved_path": str(target),\n "read": {k: v for k, v in read_payload.items() if k != "text"},\n "deterministic_summary": deterministic_summary,\n "ollama": {\n "used_for_planning": False,\n "used_for_summary": True,\n "model": model,\n "host": ollama_host,\n "summary": summary,\n "fallback_used": not bool(summary.get("ok")),\n "note": "Ollama summary failure is non-fatal; _decode_json_objects(text: str) -> list[tuple[int, int, Any]]: decoder = json.JSONDecoder() objects: list[tuple[int, int, Any]] = [] index = 0 while True: start = text.find("{", index) if start < 0: break try: obj, end = decoder.raw_decode(text[start:]) except json.JSONDecodeError: index = start + 1 continue objects.append((start, start + end, obj)) index = start + max(end, 1) return objects def _looks_like_test_suite(payload: Any) -> bool: if not isinstance(payload, dict): return False if payload.get("action") == "test_suite": return True if payload.get("profile") in {"browser", "agent", "full"} and ("steps" in payload or "browser" in payload or "agent" in payload): return True return False def extract_test_suite_payload(text: str) -> tuple[dict[str, Any] | None, dict[str, Any]]: candidates = [(start, end, obj) for start, end, obj in _decode_json_objects(text) if _looks_like_test_suite(obj)] if not candidates: return None, {"json_object_count": 0, "selected": None} start, end, payload = candidates[-1] return payload, { "json_object_count": len(candidates), "selected": {"start_offset": start, "end_offset": end}, } def _step_count(section: dict[str, Any] | None) -> int: steps = section.get("steps") if isinstance(section, dict) else None return len(steps) if isinstance(steps, list) else 0 def _failed_steps(section_name: str, section: dict[str, Any] | None) -> list[dict[str, Any]]: if not isinstance(section, dict): return [] steps = section.get("steps") if not isinstance(steps, list): return [] failures: list[dict[str, Any]] = [] for step in steps: if not isinstance(step, dict): continue if bool(step.get("ok")): continue payload = step.get("payload") if isinstance(step.get("payload"), dict) else {} failures.append({ "section": section_name, "name": step.get("name"), "status": step.get("status") or payload.get("status"), "expected_failure": bool(step.get("expected_failure")), "expected_status": step.get("expected_status"), "diagnostic": payload.get("diagnostic") or payload.get("error"), }) return failures def _find_step(section: dict[str, Any] | None, name: str) -> dict[str, Any] | None: if not isinstance(section, dict): return None steps = len(payload.get("bad_entries") or []) if isinstance(payload.get("bad_entries"), list) else None, "wrapper_folder": payload.get("wrapper_folder"), } def _section_summary(name: str, section: dict[str, Any] | None) -> dict[str, Any]: return { "name": name, "ok": bool(section.get("ok")) if isinstance(section, dict) else False, "step_count": _step_count(section), "failure_count": len(_failed_steps(name, section)), "failed_steps": _failed_steps(name, section), } def _derive_sections(payload: dict[str, Any]) -> tuple[dict[str, Any] | None, dict[str, Any] | None]: profile = payload.get("profile") if profile == "full": browser = payload.get("browser") if isinstance(payload.get("browser"), dict) else None agent = payload.get("agent") if isinstance(payload.get("agent"), dict) else None return browser, agent if profile == "browser": return payload, None if profile == "agent": return None, payload return None, None def summarize_test_suite_payload(payload: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, Any]: browser, agent = _derive_sections(payload) browser_summary = _section_summary("browser", browser) if browser is not None else None agent_summary = _section_summary("agent", agent) if agent is not None else None failures: list[dict[str, Any]] = [] if browser_summary: failures.extend(browser_summary["failed_steps"]) if agent_summary: failures.extend(agent_summary["failed_steps"]) rate_limit_telemetry = payload.get("rate_limit_telemetry") if rate_limit_telemetry is None and isinstance(browser, dict): rate_limit_telemetry = browser.get("rate_limit_telemetry") safety = payload.get("safety") if safety is None and isinstance(agent, dict): safety = agent.get("safety") return { "ok": bool(payload.get("ok")), "action": payload.get("action"), "profile": payload.get("profile"), "version": (agent or payload).get("version") if isinstance(agent or payload, dict) else None, "browser": browser_summary, "agent": agent_summary, "failure_count": len(failures), "failed_steps": failures, "rate_limit_telemetry": rate_limit_telemetry if isinstance(rate_limit_telemetry, dict) else {}, "safety": safety if isinstance(safety, dict) else {}, "package_hygiene": _package_hygiene_from(agent or payload), } def parse_service_log(path: str | Path, *, max_event_lines: int = 40) -> dict[str, Any]: service_path = Path(path).expanduser() try: lines = service_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="replace").splitlines() except OSError as exc: return { "ok": False, "path": str(service_path), "status": "read_failed", "error": str(exc), } event_lines: list[dict[str, Any]] = [] rate_limit_visible_count = 0 rate_limit_probe_count = 0 http_429_count = 0 conversation_429_count = 0 modal_text_count = 0 cooldown_line_count = 0 for lineno, line in enumerate(lines, start=1): lower = line.lower() is_rate_selector = "rate-limit" in lower or "temporarily limited access" in lower or "protect your data" in lower or "too many requests" in lower if is_rate_selector: rate_limit_probe_count += 1 if "visible=true" in lower: rate_limit_visible_count += 1 if "temporarily limited access" in lower or "protect your data" in lower or "too many requests" in lower: modal_text_count += 1 if "429" in lower: http_429_count += 1 if "conversation" in lower or "backend-api/conversations" in lower: conversation_429_count += 1 if "cooldown" in lower and ("rate" in lower or "429" in lower or "conversation" in lower): cooldown_line_count += 1 if (is_rate_selector and ("visible=true" in lower or "modal" in lower)) or "429" in lower or ("cooldown" in lower and "rate" in lower): if len(event_lines) < max_event_lines: event_lines.append({"line": lineno, "text": line[:500]}) return { "ok": True, "path": str(service_path), "line_count": len(lines), "rate_limit_probe_count": rate_limit_probe_count, "rate_limit_modal_detected": rate_limit_visible_count > 0, "rate_limit_visible_true_count": rate_limit_visible_count, "modal_text_line_count": modal_text_count, "http_429_seen": http_429_count > 0, "http_429_count": http_429_count, "conversation_history_429_seen": conversation_429_count > 0, "conversation_history_429_count": conversation_429_count, "cooldown_line_count": cooldown_line_count, "events": event_lines, } def build_test_report(log_path: str | Path, *, service_log: str | Path | None = None) -> dict[str, Any]: path = Path(log_path).expanduser() try: text = path.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="replace") except OSError as exc: return { "ok": False, "action": "test_report", "status": "read_failed", "log_path": str(path), "error": str(exc), } payload, extraction = extract_test_suite_payload(text) if payload is None: return { "ok": False, "action": "test_report", "status": "json_not_found", "log_path": str(path), "source": {"bytes": len(text.encode("utf-8", errors="replace")), **extraction}, } suite = summarize_test_suite_payload(payload) result: dict[str, Any] = { "ok": bool(suite.get("ok")), "action": "test_report", "status": "verified" if suite.get("ok") else "suite_failed", "log_path": str(path), "source": {"bytes": len(text.encode("utf-8", errors="replace")), **extraction}, "suite": suite, } if service_log: result["service_log"] = parse_service_log(service_log) return result def render_test_report_text(report: dict[str, Any]) -> str: suite: lines.extend([ f"profile={suite.get('profile')}", f"suite_ok={suite.get('ok')}", f"failure_count={suite.get('failure_count')}", ]) for key in ("browser", "agent"): section = suite.get(key) if isinstance(section, dict): lines.append(f"{key}.ok={section.get('ok')} steps={section.get('step_count')} failures={section.get('failure_count')}") telemetry = suite.get("rate_limit_telemetry") if isinstance(suite.get("rate_limit_telemetry"), dict) else {} if telemetry: lines.append( "rate_limit=" f"modal={telemetry.get('rate_limit_modal_detected')} " f"429={telemetry.get('conversation_history_429_seen')} " f"cooldowns={telemetry.get('cooldown_wait_count')} " f"planned={telemetry.get('planned_cooldown_wait_count')}" ) package = suite.get("package_hygiene") if isinstance(suite.get("package_hygiene"), dict) else None if package: lines.append(f"package_hygiene.ok={package.get('ok')} status={package.get('status')}") for failure in suite.get("failed_steps") or []: if isinstance(failure, dict): lines.append(f"failed={failure.get('section')}.{failure.get('name')} status={failure.get('status')} diagnostic={failure.get('diagnostic')}") service = report.get("service_log") if isinstance(report.get("service_log"), dict) else None if service: lines.append( "service_log=" f"ok={service.get('ok')} " f"modal={service.get('rate_limit_modal_detected')} " f"429={service.get('conversation_history_429_seen')} " f"probes={service.get('rate_limit_probe_count')}" ) return "\n".join(lines).rstrip() + "\n" PY python - <<'PY' from promptbranch_test_report import build_test_report r=build_test_report('/mnt/data/pb_test.full.v0.0.157.log', service_log='/mnt/data/promptbranch-service:0.0.157.log') import json print(json.dumps({k:r[k] for k in ['ok','status']}, indent=2)) print(json.dumps(r['suite']['rate_limit_telemetry'], indent=2)[:300]) print(r['suite']['browser']['step_count'], Implemented **v0.0.162** from accepted baseline `chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.161.zip`. ## Critical assessment The issue was real: `pb test status --json` could emit DEBUG/logging noise before the JSON payload when debug logging was active. That makes machine parsing brittle, especially when operators use `2>&1 | tee ...`. This release fixes JSON-output cleanliness only. It does **not** add source sync, artifact release, broad shell execution, or model execution authority. That remains consistent with the current control-plane model: Promptbranch controls policy, MCP provides deterministic capabilities, and write-capable paths remain gated until transactional verification is proven. fileciteturn52file0 ## What changed - Changed CLI logging default from DEBUG/INFO-prone behavior to quiet-by-default. - For commands using `--json`, debug logging is suppressed unless `--debug` is explicitly passed. - Added `logging.basicConfig(..., force=True)` so prior logging state cannot leak DEBUG noise into JSON-mode commands. - Added regression tests proving `pb test status --json` stdout parses directly as JSON even when `CHATGPT_DEBUG=1`. - Bumped version metadata to `v0.0.162`. ## Validation Passed: ```text 100 passed ``` for: ```bash pytest -q tests/test_promptbranch_cli.py tests/test_cli_parser.py tests/test_promptbranch_test_report.py ``` Passed: ```text 60 passed ``` for: ```bash pytest -q tests/test_promptbranch_mcp.py tests/test_promptbranch_artifacts.py tests/test_promptbranch_container_api.py tests/test_chatgpt_container_api.py tests/test_promptbranch_test_suite.py ``` Direct JSON cleanliness check passed: ```bash CHATGPT_DEBUG=1 python3 - [693] assistant
The likely failure is not just logging. Your shell wrapper/alias appears to emit a `+ promptbranch ...` trace line before the command output. If that trace goes to stdout, `python3 -m json.tool` sees `+` as byte 1 and fails. I’ll still patch Promptbranch defensively: JSON commands should support a strict machine-output path and the package should expose a clean `pb` console entry point if missing.

The command is intentionally read-only and relies\n on a previously captured `pb test full --json` log. [744] assistant
The bug is in your function: only the final newline goes to stderr. These two lines currently write to **stdout**: ```bash printf '+ promptbranch' printf ' %q' "$@" ``` So your pipe receives: ```text + promptbranch test status --json{...json...} ``` and `json.tool` correctly fails. ## Fix for current shell session Run this now: ```bash unset -f promptbranch 2>/dev/null unalias pb 2>/dev/null promptbranch() { { printf '+ promptbranch' printf ' %q' "$@" printf '\n' } >&2 command promptbranch "$@" } alias pb='promptbranch' ``` Now test: ```bash pb test status --json | python3 -m json.tool ``` That should work. The trace may still appear on your terminal, but it will be on stderr, not in the pipe. ## Better version: suppress trace for JSON commands I recommend this instead: ```bash unset -f promptbranch 2>/dev/null unalias pb 2>/dev/null promptbranch() { local arg for arg in "$@"; do if [[ "$arg" == "--json" ]]; then command promptbranch "$@" return $? fi done { printf '+ promptbranch' printf ' %q' "$@" printf '\n' } >&2 command promptbranch "$@" } alias pb='promptbranch' ``` This keeps your nice trace for normal commands, but JSON commands stay clean. ## Make it permanent Find where the function/alias lives: ```bash grep -R "promptbranch ()\|alias pb=" ~/.bashrc ~/.zshrc ~/.profile ~/.bash_aliases 2>/dev/null ``` Edit the matching file and replace the old function with the better version above. The parser still validates the JSON payload before a log is\n accepted as status evidence.\n """\n root = Path(path).expanduser()\n patterns = (\n "pb_test.full*.log",\n "pb_test.full*.log.*",\n "pb_test-suite.full*.log",\n "pb_test-suite.full*.log.*",\n "pb_test_suite.full*.log",\n "pb_test_suite.full*.log.*",\n )\n seen: set[Path] = set()\n candidates: list[Path] = []\n if root.is_file():\n candidates.append(root)\n elif root.is_dir():\n for pattern in patterns:\n for item in root.glob(pattern):\n if item.is_file() and item not in seen:\n seen.add(item)\n candidates.append(item)\n candidates.sort(key=lambda item: item.stat().st_mtime if item.exists() else 0.0, reverse=True)\n return [_path_mtime_payload(item) for item in candidates]\n''' new='''def _is_full_suite_log_candidate(path: Path) -> bool:\n """Return True for primary full-suite log files.\n\n `pb test status` is meant to summarize logs produced by commands such as::\n\n pb test full --json 2>&1 | tee pb_test.full.v0.0.163.log\n\n Operator-created derivatives such as `.log.report` and `.log.status` are\n outputs of report/status commands, not full-suite evidence. `v0.0.169` is accepted. Your session confirmed the intended safety behavior: default `pb src sync . --json` refused with `sync_mode_required`, upload preflight refused with `upload_confirmation_required`, local `--no-upload` packaged and verified, and the full/report flow completed for `v0.0.169`. fileciteturn86file0 Implemented **v0.0.170** from accepted baseline `chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.169.zip`. ## Critical assessment The remaining risk was that `--upload --confirm-upload` was still too easy to run accidentally after seeing a preflight. For MVP-E, a live ChatGPT source mutation should require a reviewed transaction identity, not just a boolean confirmation flag. The project model requires source/artifact writes to be transactional, verified, and state-updated only after verification. fileciteturn85file4 ## What changed Live upload confirmation now requires the transaction ID from the upload preflight. Preflight: ```bash pb src sync . --upload --json ``` returns: ```text status: upload_confirmation_required transaction_id: <id> ``` The confirm command now includes: ```bash pb src sync . --upload --confirm-upload --confirm-transaction-id <id> --json ``` If you run this without the transaction ID: ```bash pb src sync . --upload --confirm-upload --json ``` it now refuses with: ```text status: upload_transaction_id_required mutating_actions_executed: false project_source_mutated: false ``` If the ID does not match the current preflight, it refuses with: ```text status: upload_transaction_id_mismatch ``` The local path remains unchanged: ```bash pb src sync . --no-upload --json ``` still performs the verified local artifact transaction only. ## Test-suite update The agent/full profile now also checks: ```text src_sync_upload_preflight_plan ``` That validates the upload preflight contract without mutating ChatGPT project sources. ## Validation Passed: ```text 116 passed ``` for: ```bash PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 pytest -q \ tests/test_promptbranch_test_suite.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_cli.py \ tests/test_cli_parser.py ``` Passed: ```text 82 passed ``` for: ```bash PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 pytest -q \ tests/test_promptbranch_mcp.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_artifacts.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_container_api.py \ tests/test_chatgpt_container_api.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_test_report.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_service_client.py ``` Version consistency verified from ZIP import path: ```text PACKAGE_VERSION = 0.0.170 CLI_VERSION = 0.0.170 MCP_SERVER_VERSION = 0.0.170 SERVICE_VERSION = 0.0.170 MCP serverInfo.version = 0.0.170 ``` ZIP checks: ```text VERSION = v0.0.170 ZIP CRC/testzip = OK No .pytest_cache No __pycache__ No *.pyc / *.pyo No .pb_profile runtime state No logs or log derivatives No nested ZIPs No wrapper folder ``` I did not run the live browser/full suite in this sandbox. `v0.0.170` is accepted. Your session confirmed: ```text pb src sync . --json -> sync_mode_required pb src sync . --upload --json -> upload_confirmation_required pb src sync . --upload --confirm-upload -> upload_transaction_id_required pb src sync . --no-upload --json -> local package path tested pb test full/report -> v0.0.170 full suite/report verified ``` The upload preflight also produced a transaction ID and a confirm command, while the unqualified confirm path stayed non-mutating. fileciteturn89file0 Implemented **v0.0.171** from accepted baseline `chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.170.zip`. ## Critical assessment The next risk was not confirmation syntax anymore. The risk was **state advancement after failed live upload**. In `v0.0.170`, the guarded upload path could create the local ZIP and then attempt ChatGPT source upload. The weak point was that local artifact registry/state updates were not clearly deferred until project-source upload verification. For MVP-E, writes must be transactional: trigger, wait, re-read/verify, then update state only after verification. fileciteturn90file4 ## What changed in v0.0.171 For confirmed upload mode: ```bash pb src sync . --upload --confirm-upload --confirm-transaction-id <id> --json ``` the transaction behavior is now stricter: - Local ZIP may be written as part of the transaction. - If ChatGPT project-source upload verifies: - artifact registry is updated - artifact state is updated - source state is updated - If ChatGPT project-source upload fails: - artifact registry is **not** advanced - Promptbranch source state is **not** advanced - result reports upload failure instead of falsely treating the new artifact/source as current New/expanded payload fields: ```text local_artifact_written artifact_registry_updated state_artifact_updated state_source_updated upload_verification ``` Upload failure now reports: ```text status: upload_failed project_source_mutated: false artifact_registry_updated: false state_source_updated: false upload_verification.registry_update_deferred_until_upload_verified: true ``` This keeps the confirmed upload path aligned with the MVP-E acceptance criteria: before/after snapshots, collateral-change detection, transactional verification, and state update only after verified outcome. fileciteturn90file16 ## A later upload preflight could produce a confirm command that looked valid, but the confirmed upload would then fail with `local_artifact_collision` unless `--force` was added manually. That is not a source-upload bug, but it is a workflow bug before live upload testing. ## What changed `pb src sync . --upload --json` now detects local artifact collisions and makes the confirmation contract explicit. If a local artifact collision exists, the preflight now includes: ```json "confirmation": { "force_required": true, "force_reason": "local artifact collision must be intentionally overwritten before upload", "confirm_command": "pb src sync ... --upload --confirm-upload --confirm-transaction-id <id> --force --json" } ``` Also, if you try confirmed upload without `--force` while a local collision exists, the `local_artifact_collision` response now includes the corrected confirmation command. No live upload was executed in my validation. No new silent mutation path was added. ## Validation Passed: ```text 67 passed 52 passed 41 passed 41 passed ``` Covered: - CLI source-sync transaction behavior - upload preflight confirmation contract - collision handling - parser/test-suite/report/MCP/artifact/container checks Direct check: ```text promptbranch 0.0.172 collision_preflight_force: ok ``` ZIP checks: ```text VERSION = v0.0.172 ZIP CRC/testzip = OK No .pytest_cache No __pycache__ No *.pyc / *.pyo No .pb_profile runtime state No logs or log derivatives No nested ZIPs No wrapper folder package_import_metadata = verified package_hygiene = verified version_consistency = verified ``` Release artifact: [chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.172.zip](sandbox:/mnt/data/chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.172.zip) ## Test next after install ```bash pb src sync . --no-upload --force --json | python3 -m json.tool pb src sync . --upload --json | python3 -m json.tool pb src sync . --upload --confirm-upload --json | python3 -m json.tool pb test full --json 2>&1 | tee pb_test.full.v0.0.172.log pb test report pb_test.full.v0.0.172.log --json | python3 -m json.tool ``` Expected: - `--no-upload --force` → `verified_packaged` - `--upload --json` → `upload_confirmation_required` - if the artifact exists, `confirmation.force_required` should be `true` - confirm command should include `--confirm-transaction-id <id> --force` - confirm without transaction ID should still refuse - full suite should pass Do **not** run the generated confirmed upload command yet unless you intentionally want to mutate the ChatGPT Project source list.

## Critical assessment `v0.0.172` is accepted. Your run confirmed the important non-mutating and guarded-upload behavior: - `--no-upload --force` produced a verified local package. - `--upload --json` returned `upload_confirmation_required`. - The confirmation payload correctly included `force_required: true` and a confirm command containing `--confirm-transaction-id ... --force`. - `--upload --confirm-upload --json` without a transaction ID refused with `upload_transaction_id_required`. - The full suite/report path completed against `v0.0.172`. fileciteturn98file0 The remaining MVP-E risk was subtle but important: the upload transaction ID was too weak if it was based only on repo path, artifact path, version, included count, project URL, and upload mode. A file could change while the included file count stayed the same. That would let an operator confirm a preflight that no longer represented the current source snapshot. Transactional writes must be verified and state must advance only after verified persistence; stale confirmations violate that model. fileciteturn99file3 Implemented **v0.0.173** from accepted baseline `chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.172.zip`. ## What changed Added a content-bound repo manifest fingerprint to source-sync preflight. The preflight now includes: ```text before_snapshot.repo.content_fingerprint ``` The fingerprint hashes: ```text included file path file size file SHA-256 ``` The upload `transaction_id` now includes this content fingerprint. Result: ```text file content changes -> content_fingerprint changes -> transaction_id changes ``` That means a previously reviewed upload preflight becomes stale if the repo changes before confirmation. ## New safety behavior If you run: ```bash pb src sync . --upload --json ``` then change a file, and then try to confirm using the old transaction ID: ```bash pb src sync . --upload --confirm-upload --confirm-transaction-id <old-id> --json ``` it now refuses with: ```text upload_transaction_id_mismatch ``` and keeps: ```text mutating_actions_executed: false project_source_mutated: false ``` No new live upload behavior was enabled. No autonomous overwrite was added. ## Validation Passed: ```text 68 passed ``` for: ```bash PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 pytest -q tests/test_promptbranch_cli.py ``` Passed: ```text 134 passed ``` for: ```bash PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 pytest -q \ tests/test_cli_parser.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_test_suite.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_mcp.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_artifacts.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_container_api.py \ tests/test_chatgpt_container_api.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_test_report.py \ tests/test_promptbranch_service_client.py ``` ZIP checks: ```text VERSION = v0.0.173 ZIP CRC/testzip = OK No .pytest_cache No __pycache__ No *.pyc / *.pyo No .pb_profile runtime state No logs or log derivatives No nested ZIPs No wrapper folder ``` Release artifact: [chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.173.zip](sandbox:/mnt/data/chatgpt_claudecode_workflow_v0.0.173.zip) ## Test next after install ```bash pb src sync . --upload --json | python3 -m json.tool pb src sync . --upload --confirm-upload --json | python3 -m json.tool pb src sync . --no-upload --force --json | python3 -m json.tool pb test full --json 2>&1 | tee pb_test.full.v0.0.173.log pb test report pb_test.full.v0.0.173.log --json | python3 -m json.tool ``` Still do **not** run the generated confirmed upload command unless you intentionally want to mutate the ChatGPT Project source list. ## Verdict ✅ Strengths — upload confirmation is now tied to the actual repo contents, not just version/count metadata. ⚠️ Weaknesses — real confirmed upload still needs one intentional live validation later. 🔍 Unknowns — whether ChatGPT source upload remains stable under rate-limit pressure. 🧩 Next step — validate `v0.0.173`; if green, the next MVP step is a single intentional confirmed upload test with before/after source-list verification.

But it is **not safe to accept confirmed upload as complete**, because the transaction result says service error while the source-list verification says the expected file is present. For MVP-E, that should be represented explicitly as something like: ```text status: upload_ambiguous expected_source_present_after: true upload_result_ok: false artifact_registry_updated: false state_source_updated: false operator_review_required: true ``` State must still not advance until the result is unambiguous, because the project rules require transactional writes, before/after snapshots, collateral-change detection, and state update only after verified outcome. fileciteturn116file8 ## Verdict ✅ Strengths — `v0.0.175` full suite passed; confirmed upload failure is now structured, not a traceback. ⚠️ Weaknesses — confirmed upload result is ambiguous: expected source appears after upload, but service returned a 504 remove/delete failure. 🔍 Unknowns — whether the service failed while removing/replacing an existing source after successfully adding the new ZIP. 🧩 Next step — implement `v0.0.176` with explicit `upload_ambiguous` classification and no registry/state advancement when upload result and source-list verification disagree.
